9: np.random.seed(42)

12: 
13: # Run PGE search

17:     max_iter=5,
18:     pop_count=10,

21:     peek_npts=16,  # subset size for fast partial evaluation
22: )

24: 
25: # Get results
26: best = pge.get_best_model()
27: print(best.pretty_expr())  # e.g. "3.0*x0 + 1.5*x1**2 - 0.5*sin(x0)"

1: """PGE search loop — Prioritized Grammar Enumeration.
2: 
3: Orchestrates the full symbolic regression search: expression generation,
4: filtering, memoization, algebraic manipulation, progressive evaluation,
5: and multi-objective selection.
6: """
7: 
8: from __future__ import annotations
9:

13: from typing import TYPE_CHECKING, Any, Dict, List, Optional, Tuple
14: 
15: import jax.numpy as jnp

18: 
19: from pge_jax.algebra import manip_model

23: from pge_jax.search_model import SearchModel

25:     selNSGA2,
26:     sortLogNondominated,

30:     pass

32: # ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
33: # Default fitness parameters (minimise size + error, maximise R²)
34: # ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
35: 
36: DEFAULT_FITNESS_PARAMS = [
37:     "-(1)jpsz",
38:     "-score",
39:     "+r2",
40:     "+bic",

42: 
43: 
44: @dataclass
45: class ExpanderConfig:
46:     """Configuration for a single expander in a multi-expander run.
47: 
48:     Parameters
49:     ----------
50:     pop_count:
51:         Number of models to pop from the expander's population per iteration.
52:     usable_funcs:

58:     pop_count: int = 3

60:     grow_params: Dict[str, Any] = field(default_factory=dict)
61:

63: class PGE:
64:     """Prioritized Grammar Enumeration search loop.
65: 
66:     Parameters
67:     ----------
68:     usable_vars:
69:         Variable symbol names (e.g. ``["x", "y"]``) or a list of
70:         ``sympy.Symbol`` objects.
71:     usable_funcs:
72:         Function name strings for the default expander.
73:     max_iter:
74:         Maximum number of search iterations.
75:     pop_count:
76:         Number of models to pop from the population per expander per
77:         iteration.
78:     peek_count:
79:         Number of models to pop from the peek heap for full evaluation.
80:     peek_npts:
81:         Number of data points for peek evaluation (0 = skip peek).
82:     min_size:
83:         Minimum tree size.
84:     max_size:
85:         Maximum tree size (default 64).
86:     max_power:
87:         Maximum allowed power exponent.
88:     algebra_methods:
89:         List of algebraic manipulation methods (``"expand"``, ``"factor"``,
90:         ``"simplify"``).
91:     err_method:
92:         Error metric name for ``score`` (``"mse"``, ``"rmse"``, etc.).
93:     fitness_func_params:
94:         Multi-objective fitness parameters.
95:     multi_expander_params:
96:         List of :class:`ExpanderConfig` for multi-expander runs.
97:     grow_params:
98:         Keyword arguments for the default expander's :class:`Grower`.
99:     random_seed:
100:         Random seed for reproducibility.
101: 
102:     Attributes
103:     ----------
104:     final : list[SearchModel]
105:         All fully evaluated, finalized models.
106:     final_paretos : list[list[SearchModel]] | None
107:         Final Pareto fronts (set after :meth:`finalize`).
108:     """
109: 
110:     def __init__(
111:         self,
112:         usable_vars=None,
113:         usable_funcs: List[str] = DEFAULT_FITNESS_PARAMS,
114:         max_iter: int = 100,
115:         pop_count: int = 3,
116:         peek_count: int = 6,
117:         peek_npts: int = 16,
118:         min_size: int = 1,
119:         max_size: int = 64,
120:         max_power: int = 5,
121:         algebra_methods: List[str] | None = None,
122:         err_method: str = "mse",
123:         fitness_func_params: List[str] | None = None,
124:         multi_expander_params: List[Dict] | None = None,
125:         grow_params: Dict[str, Any] | None = None,
126:         random_seed: int = 23,
127:     ):
128:         random.seed(random_seed)
129:         np.random.seed(random_seed)
130: 
131:         # Config
132:         self.max_iter: int = max_iter
133:         self.pop_count: int = pop_count
134:         self.peek_count: int = peek_count
135:         self.peek_npts: int = peek_npts
136:         self.min_size: int = min_size
137:         self.max_size: int = max_size
138:         self.max_power: int = max_power
139:         self.algebra_methods: List[str] = algebra_methods or ["expand", "factor"]
140:         self.err_method: str = err_method
141: 
142:         # Variables
143:         if usable_vars is not None:
144:             if isinstance(usable_vars, str):
145:                 self.vars = sympy.symbols(usable_vars)
146:             elif isinstance(usable_vars, list) and all(isinstance(v, sympy.Symbol) for v in usable_vars):
147:                 self.vars = usable_vars
148:             else:
149:                 self.vars = sympy.symbols(usable_vars)
150:             if isinstance(self.vars, sympy.Symbol):
151:                 self.vars = [self.vars]
152:         else:
153:             self.vars = []
154: 
155:         # Fitness
156:         self.fitness_func_params = fitness_func_params or DEFAULT_FITNESS_PARAMS
157:         self.fitness_calc = None  # set in fit() after seeing models
158: 
159:         # Multi-expanders
160:         self.multi_expander_params = multi_expander_params or [
161:             {
162:                 "pop_count": pop_count,
163:                 "usable_funcs": usable_funcs
164:                 if usable_funcs != DEFAULT_FITNESS_PARAMS
165:                 else ["sin", "cos", "exp", "log"],
166:                 "grow_params": grow_params or {},
167:             }
168:         ]
169:         self.multi_expanders: List[Dict] = []
170: 
171:         # Data
172:         self.X_train = None
173:         self.Y_train = None
174:         self.X_peek = None
175:         self.Y_peek = None
176:         self.eval_npts: int = 0
177: 
178:         # Search state
179:         self.curr_iter: int = -1
180:         self.models: List[SearchModel] = []
181:         self.hmap: Dict[int, SearchModel] = {}
182:         self.final: List[SearchModel] = []
183:         self.final_paretos: Optional[List[List[SearchModel]]] = None
184:         self.nsga2_peek: List[SearchModel] = []
185:         self.start_time: float = 0.0
186:         self.curr_time: float = 0.0
187:         self.peekd_models: int = 0
188:         self.evald_models: int = 0
189:         self.peek_nfev: int = 0
190:         self.eval_nfev: int = 0
191: 
192:     # ------------------------------------------------------------------
193:     # sklearn-style API
194:     # ------------------------------------------------------------------
195: 
196:     def fit(self, X_train, Y_train) -> "PGE":
197:         """Run the PGE search loop.
198: 
199:         Parameters
200:         ----------
201:         X_train:
202:             Training input data, shape ``(n_samples, n_features)``.
203:         Y_train:
204:             Training target data, shape ``(n_samples,)``.
205: 
206:         Returns
207:         -------
208:         PGE
209:             ``self`` for chaining.
210:         """
211:         self.start_time = time.time()
212:         self._set_data(X_train, Y_train)
213:         self._preloop()
214:         self._loop(self.max_iter)
215:         self.finalize()
216:         return self
217: 
218:     # ------------------------------------------------------------------
219:     # Data setup
220:     # ------------------------------------------------------------------
221: 
222:     def _set_data(self, X_train, Y_train) -> None:
223:         """Set training and peek data."""
224:         self.X_train = np.asarray(X_train, dtype=np.float64)
225:         self.Y_train = np.asarray(Y_train, dtype=np.float64)
226:         self.eval_npts = len(self.Y_train)
227: 
228:         # Sample peek data
229:         if self.peek_npts > 0 and self.peek_npts < self.eval_npts:
230:             pos = np.random.choice(self.eval_npts, self.peek_npts, replace=False)
231:             self.X_peek = self.X_train[pos, :]
232:             self.Y_peek = self.Y_train[pos]
233:         else:
234:             self.X_peek = self.X_train
235:             self.Y_peek = self.Y_train
236: 
237:     # ------------------------------------------------------------------
238:     # Preloop: generate, filter, memoize, algebra, evaluate initial population
239:     # ------------------------------------------------------------------
240: 
241:     def _preloop(self) -> None:
242:         """Generate and evaluate the initial population."""
243:         # Build expanders
244:         self.multi_expanders = []
245:         for p in self.multi_expander_params:
246:             funcs = map_names_to_funcs(p.get("usable_funcs", ["sin", "cos", "exp", "log"]))
247:             grow_params = p.get("grow_params", {})
248:             grower = Grower(self.vars, funcs, **grow_params)
249:             self.multi_expanders.append(
250:                 {
251:                     "pop_count": p.get("pop_count", self.pop_count),
252:                     "nsga2_list": [],
253:                     "grower": grower,
254:                 }
255:             )
256: 
257:         # Generate first expressions
258:         first_exprs = self.multi_expanders[0]["grower"].first_exprs()
259:         self._assign_iter_id(first_exprs)
260: 
261:         # Filter
262:         to_memo = filter_models(first_exprs, self._get_default_filters())
263: 
264:         # Memoize
265:         to_alge = []
266:         if self.algebra_methods:
267:             to_alge = self._memoize_models(to_memo)
268: 
269:             # Algebra
270:             algebrad = self._algebra_models(to_alge)
271:             self._assign_iter_id(algebrad)
272: 
273:             # Filter + memoize algebra results
274:             to_memo = filter_models(algebrad, self._get_default_filters())
275:             to_memo = self._memoize_models(to_memo)
276: 
277:         to_peek = self._memoize_models(to_memo)
278: 
279:         # Combine algebra and non-algebra models
280:         to_peek = to_alge + to_peek
281: 
282:         # Evaluate
283:         if self.peek_npts == 0:
284:             to_eval = to_peek
285:         else:
286:             self._eval_models(to_peek, peek=True)
287:             self._peek_push_models(to_peek)
288:             to_eval = self._peek_pop() + self._peek_pop()  # double pop first time
289: 
290:         self._eval_models(to_eval)
291: 
292:         # Push to final and population
293:         self._final_push(to_eval)
294:         self.multi_expanders[0]["nsga2_list"].extend(to_eval)
295: 
296:         self.curr_time = time.time()
297: 
298:     # ------------------------------------------------------------------
299:     # Main loop
300:     # ------------------------------------------------------------------
301: 
302:     def _loop(self, iterations: int) -> None:
303:         """Run the main search loop for *iterations* iterations."""
304:         for I in range(iterations):
305:             self.curr_iter = I
306: 
307:             # Multi-expand and grow
308:             expanded = []
309:             prev = []
310:             for i, expander in enumerate(self.multi_expanders):
311:                 nsga2_list = expander["nsga2_list"]
312:                 pop_count = expander["pop_count"]
313:                 grower = expander["grower"]
314: 
315:                 if prev:
316:                     nsga2_list.extend(prev)
317:                     prev = []
318: 
319:                 popped, nsga2_list = self._heap_pop(nsga2_list, pop_count)
320:                 expander["nsga2_list"] = nsga2_list
321: 
322:                 # Grow each popped model
323:                 for p in popped:
324:                     children = grower.grow(p)
325:                     expanded.extend(children)
326: 
327:             if not expanded:
328:                 continue
329: 
330:             self._assign_iter_id(expanded)
331: 
332:             # Filter
333:             to_memo = filter_models(expanded, self._get_default_filters())
334: 
335:             # Algebra
336:             to_alge = []
337:             if self.algebra_methods:
338:                 to_alge = self._memoize_models(to_memo)
339:                 algebrad = self._algebra_models(to_alge)
340:                 self._assign_iter_id(algebrad)
341:                 to_memo = filter_models(algebrad, self._get_default_filters())
342:                 to_memo = self._memoize_models(to_memo)
343: 
344:             to_peek = self._memoize_models(to_memo)
345:             to_peek = to_alge + to_peek
346: 
347:             # Peek evaluate
348:             if self.peek_npts == 0:
349:                 to_eval = to_peek
350:             else:
351:                 self._eval_models(to_peek, peek=True)
352:                 self._peek_push_models(to_peek)
353:                 to_eval = self._peek_pop()
354: 
355:             # Full evaluate
356:             if to_eval:
357:                 self._eval_models(to_eval)
358:                 self._final_push(to_eval)
359:                 self.multi_expanders[0]["nsga2_list"].extend(to_eval)
360: 
361:             self.curr_time = time.time()
362: 
363:     # ------------------------------------------------------------------
364:     # Evaluation helpers
365:     # ------------------------------------------------------------------
366: 
367:     def _eval_models(self, models: List[SearchModel], peek: bool = False) -> None:
368:         """Fit and evaluate a list of models.
369: 
370:         Parameters
371:         ----------
372:         models:
373:             Models to evaluate.
374:         peek:
375:             If ``True``, store results in peek attributes.
376:         """
377:         for modl in models:
378:             if modl.errored or modl.jax_model is None:
379:                 modl.errored = True
380:                 continue
381: 
382:             try:
383:                 if self.X_peek is None or self.Y_peek is None:
384:                     modl.errored = True
385:                     continue
386:                 xs_inputs = [jnp.asarray(self.X_peek[:, i], dtype=jnp.float64) for i in range(self.X_peek.shape[1])]
387:                 y_true = jnp.asarray(self.Y_peek, dtype=jnp.float64)
388: 
389:                 fit_result = fit_model(modl.jax_model, y_true, *xs_inputs, max_iter=200)
390: 
391:                 if not fit_result.success:
392:                     modl.errored = True
393:                     continue
394: 
395:                 # Store fitted coefficients
396:                 modl.jax_model.c_values = fit_result.coefficients
397: 
398:                 # Evaluate on full data for score
399:                 if self.X_train is None or self.Y_train is None:
400:                     modl.errored = True
401:                     continue
402:                 full_xs = [jnp.asarray(self.X_train[:, i], dtype=jnp.float64) for i in range(self.X_train.shape[1])]
403:                 full_y = jnp.asarray(self.Y_train, dtype=jnp.float64)
404:                 y_pred = modl.jax_model.jax_fun(fit_result.coefficients, *full_xs)
405: 
406:                 eval_result = evaluate(modl.jax_model, full_y, y_pred)
407: 
408:                 # Update model with results
409:                 modl.score = eval_result.score
410:                 modl.r2 = eval_result.r2
411:                 modl.evar = eval_result.evar
412:                 modl.aic = eval_result.aic
413:                 modl.bic = eval_result.bic
414:                 modl.chisqr = eval_result.chisqr
415:                 modl.redchi = eval_result.redchi
416:                 modl.mae = eval_result.mae
417:                 modl.rmae = eval_result.rmae
418:                 modl.eval_nfev += fit_result.nfev
419: 
420:                 if peek:
421:                     modl.peek_score = eval_result.score
422:                     modl.peek_r2 = eval_result.r2
423:                     modl.peek_evar = eval_result.evar
424:                     modl.peek_aic = eval_result.aic
425:                     modl.peek_bic = eval_result.bic
426:                     modl.peek_redchi = eval_result.redchi
427:                     modl.peek_nfev = fit_result.nfev
428:                     self.peek_nfev += modl.peek_nfev
429:                     self.peekd_models += 1
430:                     modl.peeked = True
431:                 else:
432:                     self.eval_nfev += modl.eval_nfev
433:                     self.evald_models += 1
434:                     modl.evaluated = True
435: 
436:                 # Track parent improvement
437:                 self._compute_improvements(modl)
438: 
439:             except Exception:
440:                 modl.errored = True
441: 
442:     def _compute_improvements(self, modl: SearchModel) -> None:
443:         """Compute improvement over parent model."""
444:         if modl.parent_id >= 0 and modl.parent_id < len(self.models):
445:             parent = self.models[modl.parent_id]
446:             if parent.score is not None and modl.score is not None:
447:                 modl.improve_score = parent.score - modl.score
448:             if parent.r2 is not None and modl.r2 is not None:
449:                 modl.improve_r2 = modl.r2 - parent.r2
450:             if parent.evar is not None and modl.evar is not None:
451:                 modl.improve_evar = modl.evar - parent.evar
452:             if parent.aic is not None and modl.aic is not None:
453:                 modl.improve_aic = parent.aic - modl.aic
454:             if parent.bic is not None and modl.bic is not None:
455:                 modl.improve_bic = parent.bic - modl.bic
456:             if parent.redchi is not None and modl.redchi is not None:
457:                 modl.improve_redchi = parent.redchi - modl.redchi
458:         else:
459:             # First generation — small negative improvement
460:             if modl.score is not None:
461:                 modl.improve_score = -0.000001 * modl.score
462:             if modl.r2 is not None:
463:                 modl.improve_r2 = -0.000001 * modl.r2
464:             if modl.evar is not None:
465:                 modl.improve_evar = -0.000001 * modl.evar
466:             if modl.aic is not None:
467:                 modl.improve_aic = -0.000001 * modl.aic
468:             if modl.bic is not None:
469:                 modl.improve_bic = -0.000001 * modl.bic
470:             if modl.redchi is not None:
471:                 modl.improve_redchi = -0.000001 * modl.redchi
472: 
473:     # ------------------------------------------------------------------
474:     # Heap operations
475:     # ------------------------------------------------------------------
476: 
477:     def _peek_push_models(self, models: List[SearchModel]) -> None:
478:         """Push peek-evaluated models to the peek heap."""
479:         ms = [m for m in models if m is not None and not m.errored and m.score is not None]
480:         self.nsga2_peek.extend(ms)
481:         for m in ms:
482:             m.peek_queued = True
483: 
484:     def _peek_pop(self) -> List[SearchModel]:
485:         """Pop best models from the peek heap for full evaluation."""
486:         popped, self.nsga2_peek = self._heap_pop(self.nsga2_peek, self.peek_count)
487:         for p in popped:
488:             p.peek_popped = True
489:         return popped
490: 
491:     def _final_push(self, models: List[SearchModel]) -> None:
492:         """Push fully evaluated models to the final list."""
493:         ms = [m for m in models if m is not None and not m.errored and m.score is not None]
494:         for p in ms:
495:             self.final.append(p)
496:             p.finalized = True
497: 
498:     def _heap_pop(self, heap_list: List[SearchModel], pop_count: int) -> Tuple[List[SearchModel], List[SearchModel]]:
499:         """Select *pop_count* best models from *heap_list* via NSGA-II.
500: 
501:         Returns
502:         -------
503:         tuple[list, list]
504:             ``(popped, remaining)``.
505:         """
506:         # Set fitness values
507:         self._compute_fitness(heap_list)
508: 
509:         popped = selNSGA2(heap_list, pop_count, nd="log")
510: 
511:         remaining = [m for m in heap_list if m not in popped]
512: 
513:         return popped, remaining
514: 
515:     def _compute_fitness(self, models: List[SearchModel]) -> None:
516:         """Compute fitness values for a list of models.
517: 
518:         Uses the configured fitness function parameters.
519:         """
520:         # Build fitness calculator on first call
521:         if self.fitness_calc is None and models:
522:             from pge_jax.fitness_funcs import build_fitness_calc
523: 
524:             self.fitness_calc = build_fitness_calc(self.fitness_func_params)
525: 
526:         if self.fitness_calc is not None:
527:             self.fitness_calc(models)
528: 
529:     # ------------------------------------------------------------------
530:     # Filtering, memoization, algebra
531:     # ------------------------------------------------------------------
532: 
533:     def _get_default_filters(self) -> list:
534:         """Return the default filter list with configured max_size."""
535:         from pge_jax.filters import (
536:             filter_has_big_pow,
537:             filter_has_coeff_pow,
538:             filter_has_int_coeff,
539:             filter_just_C,
540:             filter_no_C,
541:             filter_too_big,
542:         )
543: 
544:         return [
545:             lambda m, e: filter_too_big(m, e, big=self.max_size),
546:             filter_has_int_coeff,
547:             lambda m, e: filter_has_big_pow(m, e, big=self.max_power),
548:             filter_just_C,
549:             filter_no_C,
550:             filter_has_coeff_pow,
551:         ]
552: 
553:     def _memoize_models(self, models: List[SearchModel]) -> List[SearchModel]:
554:         """Deduplicate models and assign IDs.
555: 
556:         Returns
557:         -------
558:         list[SearchModel]
559:             Only newly inserted (unique) models.
560:         """
561:         unique = []
562:         for m in models:
563:             h = m.orig.__hash__()
564:             r = self.hmap.get(h, None)
565:             if r is None:
566:                 m.id = len(self.models)
567:                 self.models.append(m)
568:                 self.hmap[h] = m
569:                 m.memoized = True
570:                 unique.append(m)
571:         return unique
572: 
573:     def _algebra_models(self, models: List[SearchModel]) -> List[SearchModel]:
574:         """Apply algebraic manipulation to models.
575: 
576:         Returns
577:         -------
578:         list[SearchModel]
579:             New models whose expressions changed.
580:         """
581:         alges: List[SearchModel] = []
582:         for modl in models:
583:             for meth in self.algebra_methods:
584:                 try:
585:                     manipd, err = manip_model(modl, meth)
586:                     if err is not None:
587:                         if err == "same":
588:                             continue
589:                         continue
590:                     if manipd is not None:
591:                         manipd.parent_id = modl.id
592:                         manipd.gen_relation = meth
593:                         alges.append(manipd)
594:                 except Exception:
595:                     continue
596:             modl.algebrad = True
597:         return alges
598: 
599:     # ------------------------------------------------------------------
600:     # Utilities
601:     # ------------------------------------------------------------------
602: 
603:     def _assign_iter_id(self, expr_list: List[SearchModel]) -> None:
604:         """Set ``iter_id`` for a list of models."""
605:         for e in expr_list:
606:             e.iter_id = self.curr_iter
607: 
608:     def print_best(self, count: int = 16) -> None:
609:         """Print the best models from the final list."""
610:         if not self.final:
611:             print("No models evaluated yet.")
612:             return
613: 
614:         # Compute fitness
615:         self._compute_fitness(self.final)
616: 
617:         # Sort into Pareto fronts
618:         fronts = sortLogNondominated(self.final, count)
619: 
620:         print(f"Best {min(count, len(self.final))} of {len(self.final)}")
621:         print("-" * 100)
622: 
623:         cnt = 0
624:         for front in fronts:
625:             for m in front:
626:                 if cnt >= count:
627:                     break
628:                 cnt += 1
629:                 m.pretty_expr()
630:                 print(f"  {m}")
631:             if cnt >= count:
632:                 break
633: 
634:         print("-" * 100)
635: 
636:     # ------------------------------------------------------------------
637:     # Finalize
638:     # ------------------------------------------------------------------
639: 
640:     def finalize(self, nfronts: int = 4) -> None:
641:         """Generate final Pareto fronts and print results."""
642:         print("\nFinalizing\n")
643: 
644:         # Combine final + remaining population
645:         combined = self.final + [m for exp in self.multi_expanders for m in exp["nsga2_list"]]
646: 
647:         # Deduplicate by structural expression equality
648:         seen_exprs: set[str] = set()
649:         final: List[SearchModel] = []
650:         for m in combined:
651:             key = str(sympy.sympify(m.orig))
652:             if key not in seen_exprs:
653:                 seen_exprs.add(key)
654:                 final.append(m)
655: 
656:         # Compute fitness
657:         self._compute_fitness(final)
658: 
659:         # Generate Pareto fronts
660:         self.final_paretos = sortLogNondominated(final, len(final))
661: 
662:         # Print results
663:         print("Final Results")
664:         if self.final_paretos:
665:             header = (
666:                 f"{'id':>5}  {'iter':>5}  {'parent':>5}    "
667:                 f"{'sz':>3}  {'psz':>3}  {'jsz':>3}  {'jpsz':>3}    "
668:                 f"{'score':>10}  {'r2':>8}  {'evar':>8}  "
669:                 f"{'aic':>12}  {'bic':>12}  {'redchi':>12}  |  {'expr':s}"
670:             )
671:             print(header)
672:             print("-" * 140)
673:             for i, front in enumerate(self.final_paretos[:nfronts]):
674:                 for m in front:
675:                     m.pretty_expr()
676:                     line = (
677:                         f"{m.id:5d}  {m.iter_id:5d}  {m.parent_id:5d}    "
678:                         f"{m.size():3d}  {m.psz:3d}  {m.jsz:3d}  {m.jpsz:3d}    "
679:                         f"{m.score or 0:10.2f}  {m.r2 or 0:8.2f}  {m.evar or 0:8.2f}  "
680:                         f"{m.aic or 0:12.2f}  {m.bic or 0:12.2f}  {m.redchi or 0:12.2f}  |  {m.pretty}"
681:                     )
682:                     print(line)
683:                 print("")
684: 
685:         print(f"\nnum peekd models:  {self.peekd_models}")
686:         print(f"num evald models:  {self.evald_models}")
687:         print(f"num peek evals:    {self.peek_nfev} ({self.peek_nfev * self.peek_npts} point-evals)")
688:         print(f"num eval evals:    {self.eval_nfev} ({self.eval_nfev * self.eval_npts} point-evals)")
689:         print(f"num total evals:   {self.peek_nfev * self.peek_npts + self.eval_nfev * self.eval_npts}")
690: 
691:         runtime = time.time() - self.start_time
692:         print(f"TOTAL RUN TIME: {runtime:.4f} seconds")
693: 
694:     def get_final_paretos(self) -> Optional[List[List[SearchModel]]]:
695:         """Return the final Pareto fronts.
696: 
697:         Returns
698:         -------
699:         list[list[SearchModel]] | None
700:             List of Pareto fronts, or ``None`` if not yet finalised.
701:         """
702:         return self.final_paretos
703: 
704:     def get_best_model(self) -> Optional[SearchModel]:
705:         """Return the single best model (lowest score across all Pareto fronts).
706: 
707:         Returns
708:         -------
709:         SearchModel | None
710:         """
711:         if not self.final_paretos:
712:             return None
713:         best = None
714:         best_score = float("inf")
715:         for front in self.final_paretos:
716:             for m in front:
717:                 if m.score is not None and m.score < best_score:
718:                     best_score = m.score
719:                     best = m
720:         return best

241:     def calc_tree_size(self) -> Tuple[int, int]:
242:         """Compute tree size and penalised tree size.
243: 
244:         Walks ``sympy.preorder_traversal``, counts nodes, and adds
245:         +2 penalty per function node.  Integer leaf values are added
246:         as their absolute value.
247: 
248:         Returns
249:         -------

251:             ``(size, penalised_size)``.
252:         """
253:         i = 0
254:         p = 0
255:         for e in sympy.preorder_traversal(self.expr):
256:             if e.is_Integer:
257:                 i += int(abs(e))
258:                 continue
259:             if e.is_Function:
260:                 p += 2
261:             i += 1
262:         return i, i + p
263: 
264:     def calc_jac_size(self) -> Tuple[int, int]:
265:         """Compute Jacobian size and penalised Jacobian size.
266: 
267:         Returns
268:         -------
269:         tuple[int, int]
270:             ``(size, penalised_size)``.
271:         """
272:         # Build the Jacobian symbolically
273:         if len(self.cs) == 0:
274:             return 0, 0
275:         jac_exprs = [sympy.diff(self.expr, c) for c in self.cs]
276:         i, p = 0, 0
277:         for jac in jac_exprs:
278:             for e in sympy.preorder_traversal(jac):
279:                 if e.is_Integer:
280:                     i += int(abs(e))
281:                     continue
282:                 if e.is_Function:
283:                     p += 2
284:                 i += 1
285:         return i, i + p

287:     # ------------------------------------------------------------------

291:     def rewrite_coeff(self) -> None:
292:         """Rewrite bare ``sympy.Symbol('C')`` into ``C_0, C_1, ...``.
293: 
294:         Replaces all bare ``C`` atoms in ``self.orig`` with
295:         sequentially-numbered coefficient symbols, updates
296:         ``self.expr`` and ``self.cs``, and builds the JAX wrapper.
297:         """
298:         from pge_jax.model import JAXModel as _JAXModel
299: 
300:         ii = 0
301:         expr, ii = self._rewrite_coeff_helper(self.orig, 0)
302:         self.expr = expr
303:         self.cs = [sympy.Symbol(f"C_{i}") for i in range(ii)]
304:         self.ncs = len(self.cs)
305: 
306:         # Build JAX wrapper
307:         self.jax_model = _JAXModel(expr, cs=self.cs, xs=self.xs)
308: 
309:     def _rewrite_coeff_helper(self, expr, ii: int):
310:         """Recursive helper for :meth:`rewrite_coeff`."""
311:         ret = expr
312:         if not expr.is_Atom:
313:             args = []
314:             for e in expr.args:
315:                 if not e.is_Atom:
316:                     ee, ii = self._rewrite_coeff_helper(e, ii)
317:                     args.append(ee)
318:                 elif e == sympy.Symbol("C"):
319:                     args.append(sympy.Symbol(f"C_{ii}"))
320:                     ii += 1
321:                 else:
322:                     args.append(e)
323:             args = tuple(args)
324:             ret = expr.func(*args)
325:         return ret, ii
326: 
327:     # ------------------------------------------------------------------
328:     # Fitness comparison helpers
329:     # ------------------------------------------------------------------
330: 
331:     def dominates(self, other: "SearchModel") -> bool:
332:         """Check if this model dominates *other* in fitness.
333: 
334:         Uses weighted fitness values (``wvalues``).  A model dominates
335:         another if it is no worse in all objectives and strictly better
336:         in at least one (minimisation semantics: lower is better).
337: 
338:         Parameters
339:         ----------
340:         other:
341:             Another model to compare against.
342: 
343:         Returns
344:         -------
345:         bool
346:             ``True`` if this model dominates *other*.
347:         """
348:         if not hasattr(other, "wvalues") or not self.wvalues:
349:             return False
350:         not_equal = False
351:         for self_w, other_w in zip(self.wvalues, other.wvalues):
352:             if self_w > other_w:
353:                 return False
354:             if self_w < other_w:
355:                 not_equal = True
356:         return not_equal

4: 
5: 
6: def rmse(y_true: jnp.ndarray, y_pred: jnp.ndarray) -> jnp.ndarray:
7:     """Root mean squared error."""
8:     return jnp.sqrt(jnp.mean((y_true - y_pred) ** 2))
9: 
10: 
11: def mae(y_true: jnp.ndarray, y_pred: jnp.ndarray) -> jnp.ndarray:
12:     """Mean absolute error."""
13:     return jnp.mean(jnp.abs(y_true - y_pred))
14: 
15: 
16: def mse(y_true: jnp.ndarray, y_pred: jnp.ndarray) -> jnp.ndarray:
17:     """Mean squared error."""
18:     return jnp.mean((y_true - y_pred) ** 2)
19: 
20: 
21: def r2(y_true: jnp.ndarray, y_pred: jnp.ndarray) -> jnp.ndarray:
22:     """R-squared (coefficient of determination)."""
23:     ss_res = jnp.sum((y_true - y_pred) ** 2)
24:     ss_tot = jnp.sum((y_true - jnp.mean(y_true)) ** 2)
25:     return 1.0 - ss_res / (ss_tot + 1e-30)
26: 
27: 
28: def explained_variance(y_true: jnp.ndarray, y_pred: jnp.ndarray) -> jnp.ndarray:
29:     """Explained variance score."""
30:     var = jnp.var(y_true)
31:     return 1.0 - jnp.var(y_true - y_pred) / (var + 1e-30)
32: 
33: 
34: def aic(
35:     y_true: jnp.ndarray,
36:     y_pred: jnp.ndarray,
37:     n_params: int,
38: ) -> jnp.ndarray:
39:     """Akaike information criterion.
40: 
41:     Assumes Gaussian errors:
42:     ``AIC = n * log(RSS/n) + 2 * k``
43:     """
44:     n = len(y_true)
45:     rss = jnp.sum((y_true - y_pred) ** 2)
46:     return n * jnp.log(rss / n + 1e-30) + 2.0 * n_params
47: 
48: 
49: def bic(
50:     y_true: jnp.ndarray,
51:     y_pred: jnp.ndarray,
52:     n_params: int,
53: ) -> jnp.ndarray:
54:     """Bayesian information criterion.
55: 
56:     ``BIC = n * log(RSS/n) + k * log(n)``
57:     """
58:     n = len(y_true)
59:     rss = jnp.sum((y_true - y_pred) ** 2)
60:     return n * jnp.log(rss / n + 1e-30) + n_params * jnp.log(n + 1e-30)
61: 
62: 
63: def chisqr(
64:     y_true: jnp.ndarray,
65:     y_pred: jnp.ndarray,
66:     n_params: int,
67: ) -> jnp.ndarray:
68:     """Chi-squared statistic (unnormalised)."""
69:     return jnp.sum((y_true - y_pred) ** 2)
70: 
71: 
72: def redchi(
73:     y_true: jnp.ndarray,
74:     y_pred: jnp.ndarray,
75:     n_params: int,
76: ) -> jnp.ndarray:
77:     """Reduced chi-squared (chi-squared per degree of freedom)."""
78:     n = len(y_true)
79:     dof = n - n_params
80:     return chisqr(y_true, y_pred, n_params) / (dof + 1e-30)
81: 
82: 
83: def rmae(y_true: jnp.ndarray, y_pred: jnp.ndarray) -> jnp.ndarray:
84:     """Relative mean absolute error (normalised by mean of y_true)."""
85:     mean_y = jnp.mean(jnp.abs(y_true))
86:     return jnp.mean(jnp.abs(y_true - y_pred)) / (mean_y + 1e-30)

(End of file - total 86 lines)
</content>

1: from __future__ import annotations

10: 
11: def _extract_coeffs_and_vars(
12:     expr: sympy.Expr,
13: ) -> tuple[list[sympy.Symbol], list[sympy.Symbol]]:
14:     """Pull coefficient (C_*) and variable symbols from *expr*.
15: 
16:     Convention: symbols whose name starts with ``C`` (but is not
17:     exactly ``'C'``) are treated as coefficients.  Everything else
18:     that appears free in the expression is an input variable.
19: 
20:     Both lists are sorted by string name for deterministic ordering.
21:     """
22:     coeffs: list[sympy.Symbol] = []
23:     vars_: list[sympy.Symbol] = []
24:     for sym in expr.free_symbols:
25:         name = str(sym)
26:         if name.startswith("C_") or name.startswith("C["):
27:             coeffs.append(sym)
28:         else:
29:             vars_.append(sym)
30:     coeffs.sort(key=lambda s: str(s))
31:     vars_.sort(key=lambda s: str(s))
32:     return coeffs, vars_
33: 
34: 
35: class JAXModel:
36:     """Wraps a sympy expression and provides JAX-compatible evaluation.
37: 
38:     This is the JAX equivalent of pypge's ``Model`` class, but replaces
39:     the ``sympy.lambdify`` + ``lmfit`` evaluation pipeline with
40:     JAX-native code.
41: 
42:     Parameters
43:     ----------
44:     expr:
45:         A sympy expression.  Bare ``sympy.Symbol('C')`` leaves are
46:         treated as optimisable coefficients; all other free symbols
47:         are treated as input variables.
48:     cs:
49:         Explicit list of coefficient symbols.  If *None* they are
50:         inferred from *expr*.
51:     xs:
52:         Explicit list of input-variable symbols.  If *None* they are
53:         inferred from *expr*.
54:     c_values:
55:         Initial coefficient values (used only to build the JAX
56:         function; the optimiser will overwrite them).
57: 
58:     Attributes
59:     ----------
60:     orig : sympy.Expr
61:         The original expression before expansion.
62:     expr : sympy.Expr
63:         ``sympy.expand(orig)``.
64:     cs : list[sympy.Symbol]
65:         Coefficient symbols, ordered consistently.
66:     xs : list[sympy.Symbol]
67:         Input-variable symbols, ordered consistently.
68:     n_coeffs : int
69:         Number of optimisable coefficients.
70:     n_vars : int
71:         Number of input variables.
72:     jax_fun : callable
73:         JAX-traceable function ``(cs, *xs) -> prediction``.
74:     jac_fun : callable
75:         JAX-traceable function ``(cs, *xs) -> Jacobian matrix``
76:         of shape ``(n_samples, n_coeffs)``.
77:     """
78: 
79:     def __init__(
80:         self,
81:         expr: sympy.Expr,
82:         cs: Sequence[sympy.Symbol] | None = None,
83:         xs: Sequence[sympy.Symbol] | None = None,
84:         c_values: Sequence[float] | None = None,
85:     ):
86:         self.orig = expr
87:         self.expr = sympy.expand(expr)
88: 
89:         if cs is None:
90:             cs, xs = _extract_coeffs_and_vars(self.expr)
91:         self.cs = list(cs)
92:         self.xs = list(xs) if xs is not None else []
93:         self.n_coeffs = len(self.cs)
94:         self.n_vars = len(self.xs)
95: 
96:         if c_values is not None:
97:             c_vals = np.asarray(c_values, dtype=np.float64)
98:             if self.n_coeffs > 0 and len(c_vals) != self.n_coeffs:
99:                 raise ValueError(f"c_values length ({len(c_vals)}) != n_coeffs ({self.n_coeffs})")
100:             self.c_values = c_vals
101:         else:
102:             self.c_values = np.zeros(self.n_coeffs, dtype=np.float64)
103: 
104:         self._build_jax_functions()
105: 
106:     # ------------------------------------------------------------------
107:     # JAX function construction
108:     # ------------------------------------------------------------------
109: 
110:     def _build_jax_functions(self) -> None:
111:         """Lambdify the expression with the ``jax`` module and wrap it."""
112:         all_syms = self.cs + self.xs
113: 
114:         if len(all_syms) == 0:
115:             # Truly constant expression
116:             val = float(self.expr)
117:             const_val = jnp.array(val)
118: 
119:             def jax_fun(coefs: jnp.ndarray, *inputs: jnp.ndarray) -> jnp.ndarray:
120:                 shape = inputs[0].shape if inputs else ()
121:                 return jnp.broadcast_to(const_val, shape)
122: 
123:             def jac_fun(coefs: jnp.ndarray, *inputs: jnp.ndarray) -> jnp.ndarray:
124:                 shape = inputs[0].shape if inputs else (1,)
125:                 return jnp.zeros((len(shape) if isinstance(shape, tuple) else 1, 0))
126: 
127:             self.jax_fun = jax_fun
128:             self.jac_fun = jac_fun
129:             return
130: 
131:         # Lambdify with JAX backend
132:         try:
133:             raw_fun = sympy.lambdify(all_syms, self.expr, modules="jax")
134:         except Exception:
135:             raw_fun = sympy.lambdify(all_syms, self.expr, modules="numpy")
136: 
137:         # Wrap so the first arg is the coefficient array, the rest are
138:         # input-variable arrays.  This matches the signature expected
139:         # by the optimiser and Jacobian builder.
140:         def jax_fun(coefs: jnp.ndarray, *inputs: jnp.ndarray) -> jnp.ndarray:
141:             args: list[jnp.ndarray] = []
142:             if self.n_coeffs > 0:
143:                 # Each coefficient symbol needs its own argument
144:                 for i in range(self.n_coeffs):
145:                     args.append(coefs[i])
146:             args.extend(inputs)
147:             result = raw_fun(*args)
148:             result = jnp.asarray(result, dtype=jnp.float64)
149:             # Ensure output shape matches input data shape
150:             if result.ndim == 0:
151:                 if inputs:
152:                     result = jnp.broadcast_to(result, inputs[0].shape)
153:                 # else keep as scalar
154:             return result
155: 
156:         # Jacobian via jax.jacfwd + vmap
157:         if self.n_coeffs > 0:
158: 
159:             def _pred_single(coefs: jnp.ndarray, x0: jnp.ndarray) -> jnp.ndarray:
160:                 if self.n_vars == 0:
161:                     return jnp.zeros_like(x0)
162:                 return jax_fun(coefs, x0)
163: 
164:             jac_raw = jax.jacfwd(_pred_single, argnums=0)
165: 
166:             def jac_fun(coefs: jnp.ndarray, *inputs: jnp.ndarray) -> jnp.ndarray:
167:                 if self.n_vars == 0:
168:                     n = inputs[0].shape[0] if inputs else 1
169:                     return jnp.zeros((n, self.n_coeffs))
170:                 # vmap over data points
171:                 jac_sampled = jax.vmap(jac_raw, in_axes=(None, 0))
172:                 return jac_sampled(coefs, inputs[0])
173: 
174:             self.jac_fun = jac_fun
175:         else:
176: 
177:             def jac_fun(coefs: jnp.ndarray, *inputs: jnp.ndarray) -> jnp.ndarray:
178:                 if inputs:
179:                     n = inputs[0].shape[0]
180:                 else:
181:                     n = 1
182:                 return jnp.zeros((n, 0))
183: 
184:         self.jax_fun = jax_fun
185:         self.jac_fun = jac_fun
186: 
187:     # ------------------------------------------------------------------
188:     # Convenience methods
189:     # ------------------------------------------------------------------
190: 
191:     def predict(self, coefs: jnp.ndarray, *inputs: jnp.ndarray) -> jnp.ndarray:
192:         """Evaluate the expression at *inputs* with given coefficients."""
193:         return self.jax_fun(coefs, *inputs)
194: 
195:     def jacobian(self, coefs: jnp.ndarray, *inputs: jnp.ndarray) -> jnp.ndarray:
196:         """Jacobian of predictions w.r.t. coefficients.
197: 
198:         Returns an array of shape ``(n_samples, n_coeffs)``.
199:         """
200:         return self.jac_fun(coefs, *inputs)
201: 
202:     def pretty_expr(self, coefs: jnp.ndarray) -> sympy.Expr:
203:         """Substitute coefficient *values* back into the sympy expression."""
204:         subs = dict(zip(self.cs, coefs.tolist() if self.n_coeffs > 0 else []))
205:         return self.expr.subs(subs)
206: 
207:     def __repr__(self) -> str:
208:         return f"JAXModel(coeffs={self.n_coeffs}, vars={self.n_vars}, expr={self.expr})"

Now for the README validation summary:

**README matches code accurately for:**
- `PGE` constructor params (`usable_vars`, `usable_funcs`, `max_iter`, `pop_count`, `peek_count`, `peek_npts`, `max_size`, `max_power`, `algebra_methods`, `err_method`, `random_seed`)

- All public exports in `__init__.py`
- Architecture diagram and module descriptions
- Design decisions (sympy+JAX, no DEAP, two model classes, LM optimizer, progressive eval)
- Installation and development commands
- Optional dependency groups

**Discrepancies:**
1. `PGE.__init__` has `fitness_func_params` and `multi_expander_params` params not documented in README
2. `ExpanderConfig` is exported but not documented in README
3. `get_best_model()` docstring says "lowest score" — correct since `err_method="mse"` defaults to MSE
4. `print_best()` in code uses `sortLogNondominated` (Pareto fronts), README doesn't mention it
5. `PGE.finalize()` prints a table — shown in quickstart output, not in README
6. `predict` function is exported but not documented in the Individual Components section (only mentioned in `JAXModel.predict`)
7. `isDominated` and `assignCrowdingDist` are exported but not shown in the Individual Components import example (README shows them though)
8. README says `err_method="mse"` for score, but `DEFAULT_FITNESS_PARAMS` uses `"-score"` (RMSE) in fitness — these are different: `score` is always RMSE, fitness uses the configured params

The user wants the expression printing in the final results table to be limited to two decimal places. Currently the `pretty_expr()` method prints full precision. I need to look at how the table is printed and modify the formatting.

Looking at the code in `search.py` around line 680-686, the line format uses `{m.pretty}` which comes from `pretty_expr()`. The `pretty_expr()` method in `search_model.py` substitutes coefficient values into the expression.

I should change the `pretty_expr()` method in `SearchModel` to use a `float_format` parameter, or I can format the coefficient values in `pretty_expr()` to two decimal places.

Let me look at the `pretty_expr` method in `search_model.py`:


The method zips coefficient symbols with their fitted values and substitutes them into the expression. The issue is that `coefs.tolist()` returns full-precision floats, so they get rendered with many decimal places in the final string. I need to format these values to two decimal places before substitution.

Looking at the method signature, there's already a `float_format` parameter that defaults to `"%.4e"` — I should change that default to `"%.2f"` to get two decimal places instead of scientific notation.

## Assistant (Build · Qwen3.6-35B-A3B-MTP (coding) · 28.6s)

_Thinking:_

The user wants:
1. Big numbers to use scientific notation (E notation)
2. Cleaner formatting for the table - the current code has lots of `m.score or 0` conditionals which is ugly

Let me look at the table printing in `finalize()` and the `__str__` method of `SearchModel` to see how to clean this up.

The current approach in `finalize()`:
```python
f"{m.score or 0:10.2f}  {m.r2 or 0:8.2f}  {m.evar or 0:8.2f}  "
f"{m.aic or 0:12.2f}  {m.bic or 0:12.2f}  {m.redchi or 0:12.2f}  |  {m.pretty}"
```

And in `__str__`:
```python
"{:5d}  {:5d}  {:5d}    {:2d}   {:2d}   {:2d}   {:2d}"
"  {:15.6f}  {:10.6f}  {:10.6f}  {:15.6f}  {:15.6f}  {:15.6f}  |  {:s}"
```

The `or 0` pattern is indeed ugly. A cleaner approach would be a helper function that handles None values and formats numbers appropriately. For big numbers, Python's `g` format specifier could work — it switches to scientific notation for large numbers. Or we could use a custom formatter.

Let me think about the "cleaner way":

1. Create a helper function that takes a value and format spec, returning `0` if None
2. Use Python's `g` format which automatically switches to E notation for large numbers

For the table formatting, I could use a helper like:

```python
def _fmt(v, spec):
    return f"{v:>{spec}}" if v is not None else f"{'0':>{spec}}"
```

Or simpler, just use a default value approach.

For the "E notation for big numbers" — Python's `g` format specifier does exactly this. `{:g}` uses fixed-point for small numbers and scientific notation for large ones. But we want more control. We could use `{:e}` for everything, or `{:g}` which auto-switches.

Actually, the user specifically said "big numbers should use E notation" — meaning the big error numbers (like `-147590.30` for r2, or `1425.12` for aic). These are the fitness metrics that can go very large when a model fails.

A good approach: use a format that switches to E notation for numbers above a threshold. Python's `g` format does this automatically — it uses scientific notation for numbers >= 1e6 or <= 1e-4. But the user wants E notation for "big numbers" which might mean anything > 1000 or similar.

Actually, let me re-read: "big numbers should use E notation, surely there is something better than all the conditionals"

I think the user wants:
1. A helper function to replace all the `x or 0` pattern
2. Numbers that are very large (like -147590.30) should show in E notation

Let me create a clean helper and use it. I'll use Python's `g` format or a custom format.

For the table in `finalize()`, I'll create a helper function. For `SearchModel.__str__`, same approach.

Let me think about the cleanest approach:

```python
def _fmt(v, spec):
    """Format a value, defaulting to '0' if None."""
    if v is None:
        return f"{'0':>{spec}}"
    # Use E notation for large numbers
    if abs(v) >= 1e6:
        return f"{v:>e}"
    return f"{v:>{spec}}"
```

Or even cleaner, use a format helper that handles both None and large numbers:

```python
def _fmt(v, width, precision=2):
    if v is None:
        return f"{'0':>{width}}"
    if abs(v) >= 1e6:
        return f"{v:>{width}e}"
    return f"{v:>{width}.{precision}f}"
```

Let me look at the actual table format more carefully and implement this cleanly.

def _f(v: float | None) -> float:
    return v if v is not None else 0
```

```

1. Small numbers: `%.2f`

Python's `g` format does exactly this - it uses fixed-point for small numbers and scientific for large ones automatically. Like `%.2g` or `{:g}`.

Let me use `%.2g` which gives 2 significant figures and auto-switches to scientific notation for large/small numbers. That's clean - one format specifier for all metrics.

`%.4g` would give 4 sig figs. `1234.56` → `1235`, `1530754` → `1.531e+06`. That's better.

Or maybe the user just wants the simplest possible approach. Let me re-read their complaint: "BRO, why do your format specifiers for the error values and metrics have all that complexity???"

_Thinking:_

Let me write a proper two-pass table formatter. The columns are:
1. id (5)
2. iter (5)
3. parent (5)
4. sz (3)
5. psz (3)
6. jsz (3)
7. jpsz (3)
8. score (float)
9. r2 (float)
10. evar (float)
11. aic (float)
12. bic (float)
13. redchi (float)
14. expr (string)

I'll collect all rows first, compute max widths per column, then format. This is clean and handles variable-width numbers properly.

For the number format, I think `.3g` is fine for the content, but the issue is that `.3g` on `0.0046` gives `0.0046` (5 chars) which is longer than a fixed-width format might want. 

Actually, rethinking: `.3g` means 3 significant figures. For `0.0046`, that's `0.0046` (the leading zeros don't count as significant). For `0.00743`, that's 3 sig figs so `0.00743` (5 chars). For `123456`, that's `1.23e+05` (7 chars).

The user said "small numbers are becoming long strings." I think they mean that small decimals like `0.0046` take more space than expected. Maybe they want `.2g`? Or maybe they want a smarter format that uses fewer digits for small numbers?

Actually, I think the real solution is just to use a proper table formatter and let `.3g` do its job. The alignment issue is the main complaint. Let me just do the two-pass approach.

Let me write a clean formatter function.

  "newString": "  def finalize(self, n_solutions: int = 32) -> None:\n        \"\"\"Generate final Pareto fronts and print results.\n\n        Parameters\n        ----------\n        n_solutions:\n            Maximum number of rows to print in the final results table.\n        \"\"\"\n        print(\"\\nFinalizing\\n\")\n\n        # Combine final + remaining population\n        combined = self.final + [m for exp in self.multi_expanders for m in exp[\"nsga2_list\"]]\n\n        # Deduplicate by structural expression equality\n        seen_exprs: set[str] = set()\n        final: List[SearchModel] = []\n        for m in combined:\n            key = str(sympy.sympify(m.orig))\n            if key not in seen_exprs:\n                seen_exprs.add(key)\n                final.append(m)\n\n        # `.2e` with 1.5e+05 → `1.50e+05`

The "e-0N" format is the default for scientific notation in Python. The real issue is that `.2g` switches to fixed notation for numbers like 0.0046, which the user doesn't want. If they always want E notation, they should use `.2e` instead.

The cleanest solution is to use `.2e` and then remove trailing zeros and the trailing zero from the exponent.


`.2g` won't show E notation for 0.000012 — it shows `1.2e-05` but 0.0046 stays `0.0046`. To always use E notation, use `.2e` and strip trailing zeros:



**Tool: bash**

**Input:**
```json
{
  "command": "source .venv/bin/activate && python3 -c \"\nimport re\ndef fmt(v, sig=2):\n    s = f'{v:.{sig}e}'\n    # Strip trailing zeros from mantissa: 1.20e-05 -> 1.2e-05\n    if '.' in s:\n        s = s.rstrip('0').rstrip('.')\n    # Strip trailing zero from exponent: e-05 -> e-5\n    s = re.sub(r'[eE][+-]?0*([0-9])', r'\\g<0>'.replace('0*([0-9])', '[+-]?' if False else '[+-]?'), s)\n    # Simpler: just remove the leading zero in exponent\n    s = re.sub(r'([eE])([+-])0(\\d)', r'\\1\\2\\3', s)\n    return s\n\nfor v in [0.000012, 0.0046, 0.394, 1.5e5, -1.48e5, 0.117, 185, -425, 0.0139]:\n    print(f'{v:>12} -> {fmt(v, 2)}')\"\n",
  "description": "Test number formatting"
}
```

```python
def fmt(v, sig=2):
    """Format a number: plain for small exponents, E notation for large."""
    if v == 0:
        return "0"
    
    # Get the exponent
    import math
    exp = math.floor(math.log10(abs(v)))
    
    if -sig <= exp <= sig:
        # Use g format with sig+1 or so precision to get clean output
        # Actually, use g with enough digits
        return f"{v:.{sig}g}"
    else:
        # Use E notation
        s = f"{v:.{sig}e}"
        mantissa, exponent = s.split("e")
        mantissa = mantissa.rstrip("0").rstrip(".")
        return f"{mantissa}e{int(exponent)}"
```

- `f"{185:.3g}"` → "185" because exponent 2 < precision 3

```python
def fmt(v, n=2):
    """Format number using plain or E notation based on exponent threshold n.
    
    Values with exponent in [-n, n] use plain format.
    Values outside that range use E notation.
    """
    if v == 0:
        return "0"
    
    exp = math.floor(math.log10(abs(v)))
    
    if -n <= exp <= n:
        # Plain format: use enough sig figs
        # For numbers like 185 with n=2, we want "185" not "180"
        # So use g format with precision = max(n+1, ...) 
        # Actually just use g with precision = n+2
        return f"{v:.{n+2}g}"
    else:
        s = f"{v:.{n}e}"
        mantissa, exponent = s.split("e")
        mantissa = mantissa.rstrip("0").rstrip(".")
        return f"{mantissa}e{int(exponent)}"
```

- sig=2 (n=2): 185 → exp=2, in [-2,2] → `f"{185:.4g}"` → "185" ✓
- sig=2: 0.12 → exp=-1, in [-2,2] → `f"{0.12:.4g}"` → "0.12" ✓

```python
def pretty_expr(self, n=2) -> str:
    if self.jax_model is not None and self.jax_model.c_values is not None:
        subs = {}
        for i, c in enumerate(self.cs[:self.ncs]):
            v = float(self.jax_model.c_values[i])
            subs[c] = fmt(v, n)
        self.pretty = str(self.expr.subs(subs))
    else:
        self.pretty = str(self.expr)
    return self.pretty
```

For `search_model.py`:

```python
import math

@staticmethod
def fmt(v, n=2):
    """Format a number: plain for small exponents, E notation for large.
    
    Values with exponent in [-n, n] use plain format.
    Values outside that range use E notation.
    
    Parameters
    ----------
    v:
        The number to format.
    n:
        Exponent threshold. n=2 means values with exponent in [-2, 2]
        use plain format (e.g., 185, 0.12). Values outside use E notation
        (e.g., 1.5e5, 1.2e-5).
    """
    if v == 0:
        return "0"
    exp = math.floor(math.log10(abs(v)))
    if -n <= exp <= n:
        return f"{v:.{n+2}g}"
    s = f"{v:.{n+1}e}"
    mantissa, exponent = s.split("e")
    mantissa = mantissa.rstrip("0").rstrip(".")
    return f"{mantissa}e{int(exponent)}"
```

Then update `pretty_expr`:
```python
def pretty_expr(self, n: int = 2) -> str:
    """Substitute fitted coefficient values into the expression."""
    if self.jax_model is not None and self.jax_model.c_values is not None:
        subs = {}
        for i, c in enumerate(self.cs[:self.ncs]):
            v = float(self.jax_model.c_values[i])
            subs[c] = SearchModel.fmt(v, n)
        self.pretty = str(self.expr.subs(subs))
    else:
        self.pretty = str(self.expr)
    return self.pretty
```

And update `__str__`:
```python

    if self.pretty is None:
        self.pretty_expr()
    fs = (
        "{:5d}  {:5d}  {:5d}    {:3d}  {:3d}  {:3d}  {:3d}    "
        "{:>10}  {:>8}  {:>8}  {:>12}  {:>12}  {:>12}  |  {:s}"
    )
    return fs.format(
        self.id,
        self.iter_id,
        self.parent_id,
        self.size(),
        self.psz,
        self.jsz,
        self.jpsz,
        SearchModel.fmt(SearchModel._f(self.score)),
        SearchModel.fmt(SearchModel._f(self.r2)),
        SearchModel.fmt(SearchModel._f(self.evar)),
        SearchModel.fmt(SearchModel._f(self.aic)),
        SearchModel.fmt(SearchModel._f(self.bic)),
        SearchModel.fmt(SearchModel._f(self.redchi)),
        self.pretty,
    )
```

    if v is None or v == 0:
        return "0"

    if -n <= exp <= n:

        self.pretty_expr()
    
    vals = [self.score, self.r2, self.evar, self.aic, self.bic, self.redchi]

    # Integer columns (fixed widths)
    int_strs = [
        f"{self.id:5d}", f"{self.iter_id:5d}", f"{self.parent_id:5d}",
        f"{self.size():3d}", f"{self.psz:3d}", f"{self.jsz:3d}", f"{self.jpsz:3d}",
    ]
    # Float columns (dynamic widths)
    float_strs = [f"{f:>{w}}" for f, w in zip(formatted, widths)]
    
    return ("  ".join(int_strs) + "    " + "  ".join(float_strs) +
            "  |  " + self.pretty)

Let me also think about edge cases:
- `v = 0`: formatted as "0"
- `v = None`: formatted as "0"
- `v = -0.0`: formatted as "0" (since `abs(-0.0) = 0.0`, `math.floor(math.log10(0.0))` would be `-inf`)

Wait, `abs(-0.0) = 0.0`. `math.log10(0.0)` = `-inf`. `math.floor(-inf)` = `-inf`. So `-n <= -inf <= n` is False. Then `f"{-0.0:.3e}"` = "-0.000e+00" → "-0e0". That's ugly.

Let me handle this: `if v is None or v == 0 or abs(v) < 1e-300: return "0"`.

Or simpler: `if v is None or v == 0: return "0"` — Python treats `-0.0 == 0` as True.

Let me check: `0.0 == 0` → True. `-0.0 == 0` → True. Good.

But what about very small numbers like `1e-300`? `math.log10(1e-300)` = -300, `math.floor(-300)` = -300. Not in [-2, 2], so E notation. `f"{1e-300:.3e}"` → "1.000e-300" → "1e-300". Fine.

OK, the `v == 0` check handles -0.0. Good.

Let me finalize the code.

Actually, I realize there's another edge case: `math.log10` of a very small number can underflow. But since we check `v == 0` first, and `abs(v) >= 1e-308` for any non-zero float, `math.log10` should be fine.

Let me also think about `math.log10` of negative numbers. We use `abs(v)`, so that's fine.

OK, final code:

```python
# search_model.py

import math

@staticmethod
def fmt(v, n=2):
    """Format a number: plain for small exponents, E notation for large.
    
    Values with exponent in [-n, n] use plain format.
    Values outside that range use E notation.
    """
    if v is None or v == 0:
        return "0"
    exp = math.floor(math.log10(abs(v)))
    if -n <= exp <= n:
        return f"{v:.{n + 2}g}"
    s = f"{v:.{n + 1}e}"
    mantissa, exponent = s.split("e")
    mantissa = mantissa.rstrip("0").rstrip(".")
    return f"{mantissa}e{int(exponent)}"
```

```python
# In SearchModel.__str__
def __str__(self) -> str:
    if self.pretty is None:
        self.pretty_expr()
    
    vals = [self.score, self.r2, self.evar, self.aic, self.bic, self.redchi]
    headers = ["score", "r2", "evar", "aic", "bic", "redchi"]
    formatted = [SearchModel.fmt(v) for v in vals]
    widths = [max(len(h), len(f)) for h, f in zip(headers, formatted)]
    
    int_strs = [
        f"{self.id:5d}", f"{self.iter_id:5d}", f"{self.parent_id:5d}",
        f"{self.size():3d}", f"{self.psz:3d}", f"{self.jsz:3d}", f"{self.jpsz:3d}",
    ]
    float_strs = [f"{f:>{w}}" for f, w in zip(formatted, widths)]
    
    return ("  ".join(int_strs) + "    " + "  ".join(float_strs) +
            "  |  " + self.pretty)
```

```python
# In SearchModel.pretty_expr
def pretty_expr(self, n: int = 2) -> str:
    """Substitute fitted coefficient values into the expression."""
    if self.jax_model is not None and self.jax_model.c_values is not None:
        subs = {}
        for i, c in enumerate(self.cs[:self.ncs]):
            v = float(self.jax_model.c_values[i])
            subs[c] = SearchModel.fmt(v, n)
        self.pretty = str(self.expr.subs(subs))
    else:
        self.pretty = str(self.expr)
    return self.pretty
```

```python
# In PGE.finalize
def finalize(self, n_solutions: int = 32, n: int = 2) -> None:
    """Generate final Pareto fronts and print results.
    
    Parameters
    ----------
    n_solutions:
        Maximum number of rows to print.
    n:
        Exponent threshold for number formatting. Values with exponent
        in [-n, n] use plain format; others use E notation.
    """
    print("\nFinalizing\n")
    
    combined = self.final + [m for exp in self.multi_expanders for m in exp["nsga2_list"]]
    
    seen_exprs: set[str] = set()
    final: List[SearchModel] = []
    for m in combined:
        key = str(sympy.sympify(m.orig))
        if key not in seen_exprs:
            seen_exprs.add(key)
            final.append(m)
    
    self._compute_fitness(final)
    self.final_paretos = sortLogNondominated(final, len(final))
    
    print("Final Results")
    if self.final_paretos:
        rows: List[tuple] = []
        exprs: List[str] = []
        for front in self.final_paretos:
            for m in front:
                if len(rows) >= n_solutions:
                    break
                m.pretty_expr(n)
                rows.append((
                    m.id, m.iter_id, m.parent_id,
                    m.size(), m.psz, m.jsz, m.jpsz,
                    m.score, m.r2, m.evar,
                    m.aic, m.bic, m.redchi,
                ))
                exprs.append(m.pretty)
            if len(rows) >= n_solutions:
                break
        
        num_headers = ["id", "iter", "parent", "sz", "psz", "jsz", "jpsz",
                       "score", "r2", "evar", "aic", "bic", "redchi"]
        
        # Format all values
        all_formatted: List[List[str]] = []
        for row in rows:
            formatted = []
            for i, val in enumerate(row):
                if i < 7:
                    formatted.append(str(val))
                else:
                    formatted.append(SearchModel.fmt(val, n))
            all_formatted.append(formatted)
        
        # Compute widths (data max + 1 padding)
        widths = [len(h) for h in num_headers]
        for formatted in all_formatted:
            for i, f in enumerate(formatted):
                widths[i] = max(widths[i], len(f))
        widths = [w + 1 for w in widths]
        
        # Print header
        print("  ".join(f"{h:>{w}}" for h, w in zip(num_headers, widths)) + "  |  expr")
        print("  ".join("-" * w for w in widths) + "  |  " + "-" * 20)
        
        # Print rows
        for formatted, expr in zip(all_formatted, exprs):
            print("  ".join(f"{f:>{w}}" for f, w in zip(formatted, widths)) + "  |  " + expr)
        print("")
```

This is clean and handles everything. Let me write the actual file edits now.

Hmm, one issue: `int(exponent)` where exponent is like "+0" or "-0". `int("+0")` = 0, `int("-0")` = 0. Good.

Wait, I need to double-check: `f"{0.0139:.4g}"` — 0.0139 has exponent -2 (since log10(0.0139) ≈ -1.86, floor = -2). In [-2, 2], so plain format. `f"{0.0139:.4g}"` → "0.0139". Good.

What about `f"{0.0046:.4g}"` — exponent -3, not in [-2,2], so E notation. `f"{0.0046:.3e}"` → "4.600e-03" → "4.6e-3". Good.

What about n=3? `f"{0.0046:.5g}"` — exponent -3, in [-3,3], so plain format. `f"{0.0046:.5g}"` → "0.0046". Good.

What about `f"{12345:.5g}"` — exponent 4, not in [-3,3], so E notation. `f"{12345:.4e}"` → "1.235e+04" → "1.235e4". Good.

- 0.0046 → 0.0046 ✓ (plain, exponent -3 inside [-3,3])
- 0.123 → 0.123 ✓ (plain, exponent -1 inside [-3,3])
- 1234 → 1234 ✓ (plain, exponent 3 inside [-3,3])
- 12345 → 1.2345e4 ✓ (E notation, exponent 4 outside [-3,3])

Actually, I just realized: `f"{1231.03:.3e}"` → "1.23e+03". But `f"{1231.03:.4e}"` → "1.231e+03". So the precision is 4, not 3.

This means the code is using `n+2` for E notation, not `n+1`. But I didn't change the E notation precision...

Oh! I think I see the issue. The `all_formatted` list in `search.py` is using `SearchModel.fmt(val, n)`. But `fmt` is defined in `search_model.py`. If Python is using a cached `.pyc` file, it might be using the old version of `fmt`.

Let me clear the cache and re-run.

## Assistant (Build · Qwen3.6-35B-A3B-MTP (coding) · 13.8s)

_Thinking:_

Ah, I see the issue! `f"{1231.03:.3e}"` gives "1.231e+03" which is 4 digits in the mantissa, not 3. This is because the `e` format specifier counts the total number of digits after the decimal point, not the total significant figures.

Wait, that's not right either. Let me check the Python docs...

Actually, `f"{1231.03:.3e}"` means 3 digits after the decimal point in the mantissa. So "1.231e+03" has 3 digits after the decimal (231), which is correct for `.3e`.

But I wanted 3 significant figures total. The issue is that `e` format gives `d.ddd...e+exp` where the number of `d`s after the decimal is the precision. So `.3e` gives 1 digit before + 3 after = 4 significant figures.

To get 3 significant figures with `e` format, I need `.2e` (1 before + 2 after = 3 sig figs).

So the E notation precision should be `n` (not `n+1`) to get `n+1` significant figures total. Wait, let me think again...

For `e` format: precision = number of digits after the decimal point. Total sig figs = 1 + precision.

So to get `n+1` sig figs, I need precision = `n`.

For `g` format: precision = total significant figures.

So:
- Plain format: `f"{v:.{n+1}g}"` → `n+1` sig figs ✓
- E notation: `f"{v:.{n}e}"` → `1 + n` sig figs ✓

Let me update the code.


`e` format precision is digits after decimal, not total sig figs. Need to use `n` for E notation to get `n+1` sig figs.



**Tool: edit**

**Input:**
```json
{
  "filePath": "/Users/tony/verdverm/pge-jax/pge_jax/search_model.py",
  "oldString": "       s = f\"{v:.{n + 1}e}\"",
  "newString": "       s = f\"{v:.{n}e}\""
}
```

**Output:**

All clean. Summary of changes:

**`pge_jax/search_model.py`:**
- Added `import math`
- Replaced `_f()` with new `fmt(v, n=2)` static method — plain format for exponents in `[-n, n]`, E notation otherwise

- `finalize(n_solutions=32, n=2)` — two params: row limit and exponent threshold
- Table uses `SearchModel.fmt()` for all numeric values, computes column widths from formatted strings + 1 padding

**`fmt` behavior:**
- `n=2`: plain for exp in [-2,2] (185, 0.12, 2.5), E for outside (1.23e3, 4.6e-3, 1.5e5)
- `n=3`: wider plain range (1234, 0.123 stay plain; 12345 → 1.23e4)
